\\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306: }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1. // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new exemplar.resourceName().substring(0, matchesUpTo),\\n415:                     exemplar.patternType(),\\n416:                     exemplar.principal(),\\n417: \\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. \\\"Allowed\\\" : \\\"Denied\\\");\\n263:         bldr.append(\\\" operation = \\\").append(action.operation());\\n264:         bldr.append(\\\" from host = \\\").append(context.clientAddress().getHostAddress());\\n265:         bldr.append(\\\" on resource = \\\");\\n266:         appendResourcePattern(action.resourcePattern(), bldr);\\n267:         bldr.append(\\\" for request = \\\").append(ApiKeys.forId(context.requestType()).name);\\n268:         bldr.append(\\\" with resourceRefCount = \\\").append(action.resourceReferenceCount());\\n269:         bldr.append(\\\" based on rule \\\").append(rule);\\n270:         return bldr.toString();\\n271:     }\\n272: \\n273:     private void appendResourcePattern(ResourcePattern resourcePattern, StringBuilder bldr) {\\n274:         bldr.append(SecurityUtils.resourceTypeName(resourcePattern.resourceType()))\\n275:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n276:             .append(resourcePattern.patternType())\\n277:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n278:             .append(resourcePattern.name());\\n279:     }\\n280: \\n281:     private void logAuditMessage(\\n282:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\\n283:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n284:         Action action,\\n285:         MatchingRule rule\\n286:     ) {\\n287:         switch (rule.result()) {\\n288:             case ALLOWED:\\n289:                 // logIfAllowed is true if access is granted to the resource as a result of this authorization.\\n290:                 // In this case, log at debug level. If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n308:                 }\\n309:         }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1. // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\\n377:             i++;\\n378:         }\\n379:         return i;\\n380:     }\\n381: \\n382:     private void checkSection(\\n383: Scan for any other potential\\n412:                 // prefix matches.\\n413:                 exemplar = new StandardAcl(exemplar.resourceType(),\\n414:                     exemplar.resourceName().substring(0, matchesUpTo),\\n415:                     exemplar.patternType(),\\n416:                     exemplar.principal(),\\n417:                     exemplar.host(),\\n418:                     exemplar.operation(),\\n419:                     exemplar.permissionType());\\n420:                 tailSet = need to examine the ACLs\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\n227:      */\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\n230:         Action action\n231:     ) {\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Only literal resources are supported. Got: \" + action.resourcePattern().patternType());\n234:         }\n235:         KafkaPrincipal principal = baseKafkaPrincipal(requestContext);\n236:         final MatchingRule rule;\n237: \n238:         // Superusers are authorized to do anything.\n239:         if (superUsers.contains(principal.toString())) {\n240:             rule = SuperUserRule.INSTANCE;\n241:         } else if (!loadingComplete) {\n242:             throw new AuthorizerNotReadyException();\n243:         } else {\n244:             rule = findAclRule(\n245:                 matchingPrincipals(requestContext),\n246:                 requestContext.clientAddress().getHostAddress(),\n247:                 action\n248:             );\n249:         }\n250:         logAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule);\n251:         return rule.result();\n252:     }\n253: \n254:     private String buildAuditMessage(\n255:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\n256:         AuthorizableRequestContext context,\n257:         Action action,\n258:         MatchingRule rule\n259:     ) {\n260:         StringBuilder bldr = new StringBuilder();\n261:         bldr.append(\"Principal = \").append(principal);\n262:         bldr.append(\" is \").append(rule.result() == ALLOWED ? If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n296:                 }\n297:                 return;\n298: \n299:             case DENIED:\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n308:                 }\n309:         }\n310:     }\n311: \n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n314:         String host,\n315:         Action action\n316:     ) {\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\n323:         // the first divergence point.\n324:         //\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\n327:         //\n328:         // 1. rs=TOPIC rn=gar pt=PREFIX\n329:         // 2. rs=TOPIC rn=foobar pt=PREFIX\n330:         // 3. rs=TOPIC rn=foob pt=LITERAL\n331:         // 4. rs=TOPIC rn=foo pt=PREFIX\n332:         // 5. rs=TOPIC rn=fb pt=PREFIX\n333:         // 6. rs=TOPIC rn=fa pt=PREFIX\n334:         // 7. rs=TOPIC rn=f  pt=PREFIX\n335:         // 8. rs=TOPIC rn=eeee pt=LITERAL\n336:         //\n337:         // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n340:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n341:             action.resourcePattern().name(),\n342:             PatternType.UNKNOWN, // Note that the UNKNOWN value sorts before all others.\n343:             \"\",\n344:             \"\",\n345:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n346:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n347:         AclCache aclCacheSnapshot = aclCache;\n348:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n349:         if (matchingRuleBuilder.foundDeny()) {\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n351:         }\n352: \n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\n355:         // name = \"*\". We search these next.\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n358:             WILDCARD,\n359:             LITERAL,\n360:             \"\",\n361:             \"\",\n362:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n363:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n364:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n366:     }\n367: \n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\n369:         String resource,\n370:         String pattern\n371:     ) {\n372:         int i = 0;\n373:         while (true) {\n374:             if (resource.length() == i) break;\n375:             if (pattern.length() == i) break;\n376:             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\n377:             i++;\n378:         }\n379:         return i;\n380:     }\n381: \n382:     private void checkSection(\n383:             AclCache aclCacheSnapshot, Action action,\n384:             StandardAcl exemplar,\n385:             Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n386:             String host,\n387:             MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder\n388:     ) {\n389:         String resourceName = action.resourcePattern().name();\n390:         NavigableSet<StandardAcl> tailSet = aclCacheSnapshot.aclsByResource().tailSet(exemplar, true);\n391:         Iterator<StandardAcl> iterator = tailSet.iterator();\n392:         while (iterator.hasNext()) {\n393:             StandardAcl acl = iterator.next();\n394:             if (!acl.resourceType().equals(action.resourcePattern().resourceType())) {\n395:                 // We've stepped outside the section for the resource type we care about and\n396:                 // should stop scanning.\n397:                 break;\n398:             }\n399:             int matchesUpTo = matchesUpTo(resourceName, acl.resourceName());\n400:             if (matchesUpTo == acl.resourceName().length()) {\n401:                 if (acl.patternType() == LITERAL && matchesUpTo != resourceName.length()) {\n402:                     // This is a literal ACL whose name is a prefix of the resource name, but\n403:                     // which doesn't match it exactly. We should skip over this ACL, but keep\n404:                     // scanning in case there are any relevant PREFIX ACLs.\n405:                     continue;\n406:                 }\n407: \n408:             } else if (!(acl.resourceName().equals(WILDCARD) && acl.patternType() == LITERAL)) {\n409:                 // If the ACL resource name is NOT a prefix of the current resource name,\n410:                 // and we're not dealing with the special case of a wildcard ACL, we've\n411:                 // stepped outside of the section we care about. Scan for any other potential\n412:                 // prefix matches.\n413:                 exemplar = new StandardAcl(exemplar.resourceType(),\n414:                     exemplar.resourceName().substring(0, matchesUpTo),\n415:                     exemplar.patternType(),\n416:                     exemplar.principal(),\n417:                     exemplar.host(),\n418:                     exemplar.operation(),\n419:                     exemplar.permissionType());\n420:                 tailSet = aclCacheSnapshot.aclsByResource().tailSet(exemplar, true);\n421:                 iterator = tailSet.iterator();\n422:                 continue;\n423:             }\n424:             matchingRuleBuilder.hasResourceAcls = true;\n425:             AuthorizationResult result = findResult(action, matchingPrincipals, host, acl);\n426:             if (ALLOWED == result) {\n427:                 matchingRuleBuilder.allowAcl = acl;\n428:             } else if (DENIED == result) {\n429:                 matchingRuleBuilder.denyAcl = acl;\n430:                 return;\n431:             }\n432:         }\n433:     }\n434: \n435:     /**\n436:      * The set of operations which imply DESCRIBE permission, when used in an ALLOW acl.\n437:      */\n438:     private static final Set<AclOperation> IMPLIES_DESCRIBE =\n439:         Set.of(DESCRIBE, READ, WRITE, DELETE, sessionPrincipal.getClass().equals(KafkaPrincipal.class)\n461:             ? sessionPrincipal\n462:             : new KafkaPrincipal(sessionPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), Determine what the result of applying an ACL to the given action and request\n475:      * context should be. Note that this function assumes that the resource name matches;\n476:      * the resource name is not checked here.\n477:      *\n478:      * @param action             The input action.\n479:      * @param matchingPrincipals The set of input matching principals\n480:      * @param host               The input host.\n481:      * @param acl                The input ACL.\n482:      * @return                   null if the ACL does not match. The authorization result\n483:      *                           otherwise.\n484:      */\n485:     static AuthorizationResult findResult(Action action,\n486:                                           Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n487:                                           String host,\n488:                                           StandardAcl acl) {\n489:         // Check if the principal matches. If it doesn't, return no result (null).\n490:         if (!matchingPrincipals.contains(acl.kafkaPrincipal())) {\n491:             return null;\n492:         }\n493:         // Check if the host matches. If it doesn't, return no result (null).\n494:         if (!acl.host().equals(WILDCARD) && !acl.host().equals(host)) {\n495:             return null;\n496:         }\n497:         // Check if the operation field matches. Here we hit a slight complication.\n498:         // ACLs for various operations (READ, WRITE, DELETE, ALTER), \"imply\" the presence\n499:         // of DESCRIBE, even if it isn't explicitly stated. A similar rule applies to\n500:         // DESCRIBE_CONFIGS.\n501:         //\n502:         // But this rule only applies to ALLOW ACLs. So for example, a DENY ACL for READ\n503:         // on a resource does not DENY describe for that resource.\n504:         if (acl.operation() != ALL) {\n505:             if (acl.permissionType().equals(ALLOW)) {\n506:                 switch (action.operation()) {\n507:                     case DESCRIBE:\n508:                         if (!IMPLIES_DESCRIBE.contains(acl.operation())) return null;\n509:                         break;\n510:                     case DESCRIBE_CONFIGS:\n511:                         if (!IMPLIES_DESCRIBE_CONFIGS.contains(acl.operation())) return null;\n512:                         break;\n513:                     default:\n514:                         if (action.operation() != acl.operation()) {\n515:                             return null;\n516:                         }\n517:                         break;\n518:                 }\n519:             } else if (action.operation() != acl.operation()) {\n520:                 return null;\n521:             }\n522:         }\n523: \n524:         return acl.permissionType().equals(ALLOW) ? ALLOWED : DENIED;\n525:     }\n526: \n527:     /**\n528:      * Creates a consistent Iterable on read-only copy of AclBindings data for the given filter.\n529:      *\n530:      * @param filter The filter constraining the AclBindings to be present in the Iterable.\n531:      * @return Iterable over AclBindings matching the filter.\n532:      */\n533:     Iterable<AclBinding> acls(AclBindingFilter filter) {\n534:         return aclCache.acls(filter);\n535:     }\n536: \n537:     private interface MatchingRule {\n538:         AuthorizationResult result();\n539:     }\n540: \n541:     private static class SuperUserRule implements MatchingRule {\n542:         private static final SuperUserRule INSTANCE = new SuperUserRule();\n543: \n544:         @Override\n545:       return result;\n565:         }\n566: \n567:         @Override\n568:         public String toString() {\n569:             return result == ALLOWED ? \"DefaultAllow\" : \"DefaultDeny\";\n570:         }\n571:     }\n572: \n573:     private static class MatchingAclRule implements MatchingRule {\n574:         private final StandardAcl acl;\n575:         private final AuthorizationResult Authorizer implementation starts loading its metadata.</li>\\n51:  *   <li>Broker starts SocketServer to accept connections and process requests.</li>\\n52:  *   <li>For each listener, SocketServer waits for authorization metadata to be available in the\\n53:  *       authorizer before accepting connections. The future returned by {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}\\n54:  *       for each listener must return only when authorizer is ready to authorize requests on the listener.</li>\\n55:  *   <li>Broker accepts connections. For each connection, broker performs authentication and then accepts Kafka requests.\\n56:  *       For each request, broker invokes {@link #authorize(AuthorizableRequestContext, List)} to authorize\\n57:  *       actions performed by the request.</li>\\n58:  * </ol>\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Authorizer implementation class may optionally implement @{@link org.apache.kafka.common.Reconfigurable}\\n61:  * to enable dynamic reconfiguration without restarting the broker.\\n62:  * <p>Authorizer implementation class may also optionally implement {@link org.apache.kafka.common.metrics.Monitorable}\\n63:  * to enable the authorizer to register metrics. The following tags are automatically added to all metrics registered:\\n64:  * <code>config</code> set to <code>authorizer.class.name</code>, <code>class</code> set to the Authorizer class name,\\n65:  * and <code>role</code> set to either <code>broker</code> or <code>controller</code>.\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * <b>Threading model:</b>\\n68:  * <ul>\\n69:  *   <li>All authorizer operations including authorization and ACL updates must be thread-safe.</li>\\n70:  *   <li>ACL update methods are asynchronous. Implementations with low update latency may return a\\n71:  *       completed future using {@link java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture#completedFuture(Object)}.\\n72:  *       This ensures that the request will be handled synchronously by the caller without using a\\n73:  *       purgatory to wait for the result. If ACL updates require remote communication which may block,\\n74:  *       return a future that is completed asynchronously when the remote operation completes. This enables\\n75:  *       the caller to process other requests on the request threads without blocking.</li>\\n76:  *   <li>Any threads or thread pools used for processing remote operations asynchronously can be started during\\n77:  *       {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}. Authorizer implementation starts loading its metadata.</li>\n51:  *   <li>Broker starts SocketServer to accept connections and process requests.</li>\n52:  *   <li>For each listener, SocketServer waits for authorization metadata to be available in the\n53:  *       authorizer before accepting connections. The future returned by {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}\n54:  *       for each listener must return only when authorizer is ready to authorize requests on the listener.</li>\n55:  *   <li>Broker accepts connections. For each connection, broker performs authentication and then accepts Kafka requests.\n56:  *       For each request, broker invokes {@link #authorize(AuthorizableRequestContext, List)} to authorize\n57:  *       actions performed by the request.</li>\n58:  * </ol>\n59:  *\n60:  * Authorizer implementation class may optionally implement @{@link org.apache.kafka.common.Reconfigurable}\n61:  * to enable dynamic reconfiguration without restarting the broker.\n62:  * <p>Authorizer implementation class may also optionally implement {@link org.apache.kafka.common.metrics.Monitorable}\n63:  * to enable the authorizer to register metrics. The following tags are automatically added to all metrics registered:\n64:  * <code>config</code> set to <code>authorizer.class.name</code>, <code>class</code> set to the Authorizer class name,\n65:  * and <code>role</code> set to either <code>broker</code> or <code>controller</code>.\n66:  * <p>\n67:  * <b>Threading model:</b>\n68:  * <ul>\n69:  *   <li>All authorizer operations including authorization and ACL updates must be thread-safe.</li>\n70:  *   <li>ACL update methods are asynchronous. Implementations with low update latency may return a\n71:  *       completed future using {@link java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture#completedFuture(Object)}.\n72:  *       This ensures that the request will be handled synchronously by the caller without using a\n73:  *       purgatory to wait for the result. If ACL updates require remote communication which may block,\n74:  *       return a future that is completed asynchronously when the remote operation completes. This enables\n75:  *       the caller to process other requests on the request threads without blocking.</li>\n76:  *   <li>Any threads or thread pools used for processing remote operations asynchronously can be started during\n77:  *       {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}.                 }};\n213: \n214:         boolean hasWildCardAllow = false;\n215: \n216:         KafkaPrincipal principal = new KafkaPrincipal(\n217:             requestContext.principal().getPrincipalType(),\n218:             requestContext.principal().getName());\n219:         String hostAddr = requestContext.clientAddress().getHostAddress();\n220: \n221:
